    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">سَبَحَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">سَبْحٌ</foreign> (Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">سِبَاحَةٌ</foreign>, (S, * K,) or the latter is a simple subst., (Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He swam,</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">عَامَ</foreign>, (S, * K,) <foreign lang="ar">بِالنَّهْرِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فِيهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">in the river</hi>], (K,) or rather <foreign lang="ar">بِالمَآءِ</foreign> (MF, TA) or <foreign lang="ar">فى المَآءِ</foreign> (Msb) [i. e. <hi rend="ital">in the water</hi>], for it is likewise in the sea, and in a pool, and also in any expanse: (MF, TA:) [or <hi rend="ital">he swam upon the surface, without immersing himself;</hi> for,] accord. to Z, there is a difference between <foreign lang="ar">عَوْمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سِبَاحَةٌ</foreign>; the former signifying the “ coursing along in water with immersion of oneself; ” and the latter, the <hi rend="ital">coursing along upon water without immersion of oneself.</hi> (MF, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">النُّجُومُ تَسْبَحُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى الفَلَكِ</foreign> (A, TA) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The stars</hi> [<hi rend="ital">swim,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">glide along,</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">pass along, in the firmament, with a spreading forth.</hi> (TA.) It is said in the Kur xxi. 34 and xxxvi. 40, with reference to the sun and the moon, (Bd and Jel in xxi. 34,) with which the stars are meant to be included, (Jel ibid.,) <foreign lang="ar">كُلٌّ فِى فَلَكٍ يَسْبَحُونَ</foreign>, i. e. <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">All</hi> [<hi rend="ital">glide</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">travel along swiftly,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">in a firmament,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">like the swimmer</hi> (Bd and Jel ibid.) <hi rend="ital">upon the surface of the water,</hi> (Bd ibid.,) or <hi rend="ital">in the water;</hi> (Jel ibid.;) wherefore the form of the verb used is that which is appropriate to rational beings, (Bd and Jel ibid.,) swimming being the act of such beings. (Bd ibid.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And [hence] one says, <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ ذِكْرُكَ  <ref cref="n18662-1" target="مَسَابِحَ" n="1" type="6" subtype="FTFSO" lang="ar"/> الشَّمْسِ وَ القَمَرِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Thy fame has travelled as far as the sun and the moon;</hi> lit., <hi rend="ital">swum along the tracts along which swim the sun and the moon</hi>]. (A, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence, likewise, as inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign>, aor. as above,] <foreign lang="ar">سَبْحٌ</foreign> also signifies <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  The <hi rend="ital">running</hi> of a horse (S, L, K, * TA) <hi rend="ital">in which the fore legs are stretched forth well</hi> [<hi rend="ital">like as are the arms of a man in swimming</hi>]. (L, K, * TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">being quick,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">swift.</hi> (MF.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">being,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">becoming, remote.</hi> (MF.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">travelling far.</hi> (K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِى الأَرْضِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He went,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">travelled, far, in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">into, the land,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">country:</hi> (O, TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">سَبَخَ</foreign>: both thus expl. by Abu-l-Jahm El-Jaafaree. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">journeying for the purpose of traffic</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">تَقَلُّب</foreign> [q. v.]); and [a people's] <hi rend="ital">becoming scattered,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dispersed, in the land,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">earth.</hi> (K.) And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">busying oneself in going to and fro,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seeking gain,</hi> (IAar, TA,) and <hi rend="ital">occupying oneself according to his own judgment</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discretion, in the disposal</hi> or <hi rend="ital">management of affairs, in respect of the means of subsistence.</hi> (IAar, S, K, TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَسْبَحُ النَّهَارَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كُلَّهُ فِى طَلَبِ المَعَاشِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Such a one busies himself in going to and fro,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">occupies himself according to his own judgment</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discretion, in seeking the means of subsistence</hi>]. (A, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ فِى حَوَائِجِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He occupied himself according to his own judgment</hi> or <hi rend="ital">discretion in the accomplishment of his needful affairs.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  As used in the Kur [lxxiii. 7], where it is said, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ لَكَ فِى النَّهَارِ سَبْحًا طَوِيلًا</foreign>, it is variously explained: (S, TA:) accord. to Katádeh (S) and El-Muärrij, (S, TA,) the meaning is, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Verily thou hast in the day-time</hi>] <hi rend="ital">long freedom from occupation;</hi> (S, K, * TA;) and in this sense, also, its verb is <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">سَبَحَ</orth>
                  </form>: (JM:) [thus it has two contr. significations:] or, accord. to Lth, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">leisure for sleep:</hi> (TA:) accord. to AO, the meaning is, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">long-continued scope,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">room, for free action;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">مُتَقَلَّبًا طَوِيلًا</foreign>: and accord. to ElMuärrij, it means also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">coming and going:</hi> (S, TA:) accord. to Fr, the meaning is, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">thou hast in the day-time the accomplishment of thy needful affairs:</hi> (TA:) or the meaning is, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">long</hi>] <hi rend="ital">occupation of thyself in thy affairs of business;</hi> not being free from occupation therein for the reciting of the Kur-án. (Jel.) Some read <foreign lang="ar">سَبْخًا</foreign>, which has nearly the same meaning as <foreign lang="ar">سَبْحًا</foreign>. (Zj, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  As inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign>, (TK,) it signifies also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The state of <hi rend="ital">sleeping.</hi> (K.) And as such also, (TK,) <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">being still, quiet,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">motionless.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  [Also <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">glistening</hi> of the mirage.] You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ السَّرَابُ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">الآلُ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">لَمَعَ</foreign> [i. e. <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The mirage glistened</hi>]. (O.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">digging,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">burrowing,</hi> in the earth, or ground. (K, * TA.) You say of the jerboa, <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ فِى الأَرْضِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He dug,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">burrowed, in the earth,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ground.</hi> (O, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  And <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  The <hi rend="ital">being profuse</hi> in speech. (K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ فِى الكَلَامِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He was profuse in speech.</hi> (O, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  See also the next paragraph. in two places.    </entryFree>26:T2456,<entryFree id="n18663" key="تَسْبِيحٌ" type="main">

                     <itype>2</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">تَسْبِيحٌ</orth>

                  </form> signifies The <hi rend="ital">declaring</hi> [God] <hi rend="ital">to be far removed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free, from every imperfection</hi> or <hi rend="ital">impurity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from everything derogatory from</hi> [his] <hi rend="ital">glory;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">تَنْزِيهٌ</foreign>, (S, O, Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">تَقْدِيسٌ</foreign>: (Msb:) the <hi rend="ital">magnifying, celebrating, lauding,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">praising,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">glorifying,</hi> God; and <hi rend="ital">declaring</hi> Him <hi rend="ital">to be far removed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free, from everything evil.</hi> (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">سَبَّحَ ٱللّٰهَ</foreign>, (T, A, Mgh, Msb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">سبّح لِلّٰهِ</foreign>, (Kur lvii. 1 &amp;c., and A,) in which the <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> is redundant, (Jel in lvii. 1 &amp;c.,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَسْبِيحٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانٌ</foreign> is a subst. that [sometimes] stands in the place of the inf. n., (T, TA,) or it is an inf. n. of which the verb is <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign>, (K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He declared God to be far removed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free, from every imperfection</hi> or <hi rend="ital">impurity</hi> &amp;c., (A, Mgh, TA,) or <hi rend="ital">from what they say</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of Him</hi>] <hi rend="ital">who disacknowledge</hi> [<hi rend="ital">his attributes</hi>]; (Msb;) [i. e. <hi rend="ital">he declared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">celebrated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extolled, the perfection</hi> or <hi rend="ital">purity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">absolute glory, of God;</hi>] and <hi rend="ital">he magnified, celebrated, lauded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">praised, God, by the mention of his names, saying</hi>

                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سُبْحَانٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> is the inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign> as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">سَبَّحَ</foreign> [q. v.]; (K, TA;) and is a subst. that [sometimes] stands in the place of the inf. n. of the latter of these verbs, i. e. in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">تَسْبِيحٌ</foreign>. (T, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ</foreign> is a proper name in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">التَّسْبِيح</foreign>, and [for this reason, and also because it ends with <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign>,] it is imperfectly decl., and is also invariable; being put in the accus. case in the manner of an inf. n. (Mgh.) You say <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">I declare</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">celebrate</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extol</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the remoteness,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">freedom, of God</hi> [<hi rend="ital">from every imperfection</hi> or <hi rend="ital">impurity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from everything derogatory from his glory,</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">from the imputation of there being any equal to Him, or any companion, or anything like unto Him, or anything contrary to Him;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from everything that should not be imputed to Him:</hi> (L:) [<hi rend="ital">I declare,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">celebrate,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extol, his absolute perfection</hi> or <hi rend="ital">glory</hi> or <hi rend="ital">purity:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">extolled be his absolute perfection</hi> &amp;c.:] or <hi rend="ital">I declare the remoteness of God,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his freedom</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">بَرَآءَة</foreign>), <hi rend="ital">from evil,</hi> (Zj, * S, K, TA,) or <hi rend="ital">from every evil;</hi> (TA;) and [especially] <hi rend="ital">from the imputation of his having a female companion, and offspring:</hi> (K:) or <hi rend="ital">I declare God's being very far removed from all the foul imputations of those who assert a plurality of gods:</hi> (MF:) [it sometimes implies wonder, and may well be rendered <hi rend="ital">how far is God from every imperfection!</hi> &amp;c.:] in this case, <foreign lang="ar">سبحان</foreign> is a determinate noun; (K;) i. e., a generic proper name, for <foreign lang="ar">التَّسْبِيح</foreign>, like as <foreign lang="ar">بَرَّةُ</foreign> is for <foreign lang="ar">البِرُّ</foreign>. (MF:) Zj says, (TA,) it is put in the accus. case in the manner of an inf. n.; (S, K;) i. e., as the absolute complement of a verb understood; the phrase with the verb supplied being <foreign lang="ar">أُسَبِّحُ ٱللّٰهَ سُبْحَانَهُ</foreign>; (MF;) meaning <foreign lang="ar">أُبَرِّئُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهَ مِنَ السُّوْءِ بَرَآءَةً</foreign>; (S, K, MF;) <foreign lang="ar">سبحان</foreign> thus supplying the place of the verb: accord. to Ibn-El-Hájib and others, when it is prefixed to another noun or pronoun, governing it in the gen. case, it is a quasi-inf. n.; and when not so prefixed, it is a proper name, imperfectly decl.: but to this it is objected that a proper name may be thus prefixed for the purpose of distinction, as in the instances of <foreign lang="ar">حَاتِمُ طَيِّئٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدُ الفَوَارِسِ</foreign>: some say that it is an inf. n. of an obsolete verb; but this assertion is not to be regarded; for, as an inf. n., its verb is <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">شَكَرَ</foreign> of which the inf. n. is <foreign lang="ar">شُكْرَانٌ</foreign>: others say that it may be an inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">سَبَّحَ</foreign>, though far from being agreeable with analogy: and some derive it from <foreign lang="ar">السَّبْحُ</foreign> as signifying “ the act of swimming, ” or “ the being quick, or swift, ” or “ the being, or becoming, remote, ” &amp;c.: (MF:) [hence F adds,] or the phrase above-mentioned denotes quickness in betaking oneself to God, and agility in serving, or obeying, Him; [and therefore may be rendered <hi rend="ital">I betake myself quickly to the service of God, and am prompt in obeying Him;</hi>] (K;) so accord. to ISh, to whom a man presented himself in a dream, and indicated this explanation of the phrase, deriving it from <foreign lang="ar">سَبَحَ الفَرَسُ</foreign> [“ the horse ran stretching forth his fore legs, as one does with his arms in swimming ”]. (L.) <foreign lang="ar">فَسُبْحَانَ ٱللّٰهِ حِينَ تُمْسُونَ وَحِينَ تُصْبِحُونُ</foreign>, [in which <foreign lang="ar">سبحان</foreign> is used in the place of the inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">سَبَّحَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">سَبِّحُوا</foreign> is understood before it,] in the Kur [xxx. 16], means <hi rend="ital">Therefore perform ye prayer to God</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">declare ye the remoteness of God from every imperfection</hi> &amp;c.] <hi rend="ital">when ye enter upon the time of evening and when ye enter upon the time of daybreak.</hi> (Fr, TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ ٱللّٰهِ عَمَّا يَصِفْونَ</foreign>, in the Kur xxiii. 93, means <hi rend="ital">Far</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">how far</hi>] <hi rend="ital">is God from that</hi> by <hi rend="ital">which they describe</hi> Him! (Jel.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَكَ ٱللّٰهُمَّ وَبِحَمْدِكَ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">سَبَّحْتُكَ بِجَمِيعِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">آلَائِكَ وَبِحَمْدِكَ سَبَّحْتُكَ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I glorify Thee by</hi> 
                  <pb n="1291"/> enumerating <hi rend="ital">all thy benefits, and by the praising of Thee I glorify Thee</hi>]. (Mgh. [See also the prep. <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ مِنْ كَذَا</foreign>, (Msb, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ ٱللّٰهِ مِنْ كَذَا</foreign>, (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ مِنْ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, (A,) are <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  phrases expressive of wonder (S, A, Msb, K) at a thing (S, Msb, K) and a person; (A;) originating from God's being glorified (<foreign lang="ar">أَنْ يُسَبَّحَ ٱللّٰهُ</foreign>) at the sight of what is wonderful of his works, and afterwards, by reason of its being frequently said, employed in relation to anything at which one wonders; (Er-Radee, TA;) meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">I wonder greatly</hi> (lit., <hi rend="ital">with wondering</hi>) <hi rend="ital">at such a thing</hi> and <hi rend="ital">such a person;</hi> as is shown by what follows; or] <hi rend="ital">how extraordinary,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">strange, is such a thing</hi> [and <hi rend="ital">such a person!</hi>]. (Msb.) El-Aashà says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">أَقُولُ لَمَّا جَآءَنِى فَخْرُهُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ مِنْ عَلْقَمَةَ الفَاخِر</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (S, Msb *) <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">I saying, when his boasting reached me, I wonder greatly at' Alkameh the boasting</hi>]; i. e. <foreign lang="ar">العَجَبُ مِنْهُ</foreign>, (S,) or [rather] <foreign lang="ar">عَجَبًا لَهُ</foreign> [for <foreign lang="ar">أَعْجَبُ عَحَبًا لَهُ</foreign>], lit. <hi rend="ital">I wonder with wondering at him;</hi> (Msb;) [or <hi rend="ital">how extraordinary a person is 'Alkameh the boasting !:</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">سبحان</foreign> being without tenween because it is regarded by them as a determinate noun, and having a resemblance to a fem. noun: (S:) [though in what quality it resembles a fem. noun, except in its being of one of the measures of broken pls., I do not know:] or it is imperfectly decl. because it is a determinate noun, being a proper name for <foreign lang="ar">البَرَآءَة</foreign> (IJ, IB) and <foreign lang="ar">التَّنْزِيه</foreign>, (IJ,) and because of the addition of the <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ن</foreign>: (IJ, IB:) this is the true reason: but some hold that it is rendered determinate by its being prefixed to a noun understood, governing it in the gen. case; the complete phrase being <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ ٱللّٰهِ مِنْ عَلْقَمَةَ</foreign>. (MF.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانًا</foreign>, thus with tenween, as an indeterminate noun, occurs in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَهُ ثُمَّ سُبْحَانًا</foreign>, in a poem of Umeiyeh. (IB.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَان</foreign> is also used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">نَفْس</foreign>, in the saying <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتَ أَعْلَمُ بِمَا فِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانِكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Thou art possessed of more,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">most, knowledge of that which is in thine own mind</hi>]. (K.)    </entryFree>2a:T9bd,<entryFree id="n18672" key="سُبُّوحٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">سُبُّوحٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, also pronounced <foreign lang="ar">سَبُّوحٌ</foreign>, (T, S, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) the latter the more agreeable with analogy, but the former the more common, (Th, T, S, Msb, *) one of the epithets applied to God, (T, S, A, Msb, * K,) because He is an object of <foreign lang="ar">تَسْبِيح</foreign>, (K,) and [often] immediately followed by <foreign lang="ar">قُدُّوسٌ</foreign>, (A, Msb, K,) which is likewise also pronounced <foreign lang="ar">قَدُّوسٌ</foreign>, though the former pronunciation is the more common: (Th, T, S, Msb: *) it signifies [<hi rend="ital">All-perfect, all-pure,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">all-glorious;</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">far removed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">free, from everything evil,</hi> (Zj, Mgh, Msb, TA,) <hi rend="ital">and from every imperfection</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and the like</hi>]. (Msb. [See 2, and see also <foreign lang="ar">سُبْحَانَ ٱللّٰهِ</foreign>.]) It is said (S, Msb) by Th (S) that there is no word like the two epithets above, of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فعُّول</foreign> with damm as well as with fet-h to the first letter, except <foreign lang="ar">ذرّوح</foreign>: (S, Msb:) but the following similar instances have been pointed out: <foreign lang="ar">ستّوق</foreign> among epithets, and <foreign lang="ar">ذرّوح</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شبّوط</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فرّوج</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سفّود</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كلّوب</foreign> among substs. (TA.) Sb says, <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ فِى الكَلَامِ فُعَّوْلٌ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِوَاحِدَةٍ</foreign> [expl. voce <foreign lang="ar">ذُرَّاحٌ</foreign>]: (S:) [or] accord. to AHei, Sb said that there is no epithet of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فُعُّولٌ</foreign> except <foreign lang="ar">سُبُّوحٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">قُدُّوسٌ</foreign>: Lh mentions <foreign lang="ar">سُتُّوقٌ</foreign> also, as an epithet applied to a <foreign lang="ar">دِرْهَم</foreign>, as well as <foreign lang="ar">سَتُّوقٌ</foreign>.
